**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:

Elections, political figures, and government actions

It's moderated to focus on U.S.-centric content and generally avoids memes or low-effort posts. The subreddit can have a progressive or liberal-leaning tone, depending on the community's engagement, though it hosts a range of political perspectives.

### **Daily Briefing for Congressional Leadership**
**July 5, 2025**

**AREA 1: THE OMNIBUS BUDGET & POLICY BILL ("BIG BEAUTIFUL BILL")**

**Topic 1.1: Passage, General Provisions, and White House Promotion**
President Trump has officially signed into law the massive omnibus budget bill, which he has publicly termed the "big beautiful bill" [1]. The signing reportedly took place during the White House's July 4th picnic. Characterized by sources as a "megabill," the legislation enacts sweeping tax and spending cuts while simultaneously slashing Medicaid funding and increasing the national debt [2]. Given the bill's breadth and complexity, several news organizations have published explainers and guides to help the public understand its full scope, including various "little-known items" embedded within its text [3].

### **Daily Briefing for Congressional Leadership**
**July 5, 2025**

**AREA 1: THE OMNIBUS BUDGET & POLICY BILL ("BIG BEAUTIFUL BILL")**

**Topic 1.1: Passage, General Provisions, and White House Promotion**
President Trump has officially signed into law the massive omnibus budget bill, a legislative package that enacts sweeping tax and spending cuts while simultaneously slashing Medicaid funding and increasing the national debt [1]. The signing reportedly took place during the White House's July 4th picnic. President Trump has publicly termed the legislation his "big beautiful bill" [2]. Given the bill's breadth and complexity, news organizations have begun publishing explainers to help the public understand its full scope, including various "little-known items" embedded within its text [3].

**References:**
[1] Trump signs megabill that slashes taxes, Medicaid while boosting national debt, https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2025/07/04/donald-trump-signs-megabill-taxes-medicaid-border/84470497007/

[2] Trump to sign 'big beautiful bill' and #MeToo setback in Sean Combs' trial: Morning Rundown, https://www.nbcnews.com/news/us-news/trump-big-beautiful-bill-metoo-sean-combs-trial-morning-rundown-rcna216923

[3] What’s in Trump’s big bill that passed Congress and will soon become law, https://apnews.com/article/what-is-republican-trump-tax-bill-f65be44e1050431a601320197322551b

**Topic 1.2: Economic Impacts (Taxes, Debt, and Deficit)**
Passage of the bill has triggered immediate economic warnings from multiple quarters. Some economists are labeling the resulting deficit increase as "dangerous" for the U.S. economy [1]. This concern is amplified by the new reality of the national debt, which has now reached $36 trillion [2]. The bill’s spending cuts are not limited to fiscal metrics; scientists are also raising alarms that the reductions could cause the country to "lose a generation of talent" in key research fields [3]. At a regional level, one analysis concludes that despite specific provisions secured by Senator Lisa Murkowski, her constituents in Alaska are still projected to "suffer" under the new tax framework [4].

**References:**
[1] Why some economists say the deficit increase in Trump’s bill is dangerous, https://abcnews.go.com/Politics/economists-deficit-increase-trumps-bill-dangerous/story?id=123481401O

[2] How our $36 trillion debt came to be, https://www.marketplace.org/story/2025/07/01/how-did-the-36-trillion-national-debt-come-to-be

[3] Scientists warn US will lose a generation of talent because of Trump cuts, https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2025/jul/03/national-science-foundation-trump-cuts

[4] Despite Lisa Murkowski’s Deals, Alaskans Will Suffer Under Trump’s Tax Bill, https://www.huffpost.com/entry/lisa-murkowski-alaska-suffer-trump-tax-bill_n_68658de4e4b0c546723f85ff?utm_medium=Social&utm_source=reddit&utm_campaign=us_main

**Topic 1.3: Healthcare & Social Program Impacts**
A central and highly consequential component of the new law is a reported $1 trillion cut to Medicaid funding over the next decade [1]. This has led rural hospitals, which are heavily reliant on Medicaid reimbursement, to brace for severe financial impacts that could include widespread closures. The effects of these cuts are expected to be felt most acutely and immediately in rural communities across the nation [2]. The administration's Social Security Chief has reportedly praised the bill, even as critics claim its fiscal structure will ultimately damage the program’s long-term financial stability [3].

**References:**
[1] Rural hospitals brace for financial hits or even closure under Republicans' $1 trillion Medicaid cut, https://apnews.com/article/medicaid-tax-cuts-rural-hospitals-nebraska-kentucky-cf6bb787fc6a4d387c55d90051ff2f1f

[2] Trump’s Medicaid cuts are coming for rural Americans: ‘It’s going to have to hit them first’, https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2025/jul/04/rural-americans-medicaid-cuts-trump-bill

[3] Trump Social Security Chief Applauds Budget Bill That Will Harm Social Security's Finances, https://www.commondreams.org/news/trump-social-security-budget-bill

**Topic 1.4: Immigration Policy & Enforcement**
The omnibus bill allocates historic levels of funding designed to "supercharge" federal immigration enforcement operations [1]. In response to this new financial empowerment, Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE) is reportedly preparing for a nationwide "detention blitz," an action expected to cause a dramatic surge in the number of detainees held in federal custody [2]. This escalation is raising concerns that a spike in deaths within ICE facilities is now "inevitable" [3].

**References:**
[1] How Trump's Tax Cut And Policy Bill Aims To 'Supercharge' Immigration Enforcement, https://www.npr.org/2025/07/03/g-s1-75609/big-beautiful-bill-ice-funding-immigration

[2] ICE prepares detention blitz with historic funding from Trump bill, https://www.washingtonpost.com/business/2025/07/04/trump-bill-ice-immigrant-detention/

[3] More ICE Deaths 'Inevitable' as Detention Numbers Soar, https://www.newsweek.com/ice-detention-center-migrant-deaths-rising-2093770

**Topic 1.5: Political & Public Reaction**
The passage of the bill has reshaped the political landscape. Democratic strategists reportedly view the legislation's controversial provisions not as a defeat, but as a "key to their comeback" and a clear "Path to Win Back Voters" in future elections [1]. The public relations "battle to sway voters" over the bill's merits is now underway [2]. Polling on the bill is reportedly so negative that the President is scrambling to mount a more effective defense of its contents [3]. Commentator James Carville offered a particularly severe forecast, predicting that Republicans' passage of the bill will be remembered as a "'mass extinction event'" for the party [4].

**References:**
[1] In Trump’s Bill, Democrats See a Path to Win Back Voters, https://www.nytimes.com/2025/07/03/us/politics/democrats-trump-bill.html

[2] The battle to sway voters over Trump’s ‘big, beautiful bill’ begins, https://www.cnn.com/2025/07/04/politics/democrats-messaging-trump-big-beautiful-bill?cid=ios_app

[3] Trump Scrambles to Defend His Megabill After Savage Polling, https://www.thedailybeast.com/trump-scrambles-to-defend-his-megabill-after-savage-polling/

[4] Carville: GOP megabill passage will be seen as ‘mass extinction event’, https://thehill.com/homenews/media/5385440-carville-predicts-democrats-gain-in-2026/

**AREA 2: FOREIGN AFFAIRS & INTERNATIONAL TRADE**

**Topic 2.1: Tariff Policies & Trade Disputes**
The administration is preparing a significant escalation in its trade policy, with plans to begin notifying countries of new tariffs on their goods that could be as high as 70% [1]. This aggressive stance has already manifested in a specific threat to the European Union, which faces a potential 17% tariff on food exports to the United States [2]. These actions are prompting swift international reactions. India has already initiated a formal process at the World Trade Organization to impose retaliatory duties on U.S. automobiles in response to the administration's tariff plans [3].

**References:**
[1] Trump Plans to Start Notifying Countries of US Tariffs Up to 70%, https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2025-07-03/trump-says-he-may-start-telling-nations-new-tariff-rates-friday

[2] US threatens EU with 17% tariff on food exports, https://www.ft.com/content/d947b21a-18a4-473a-8dd1-e01920c4b644

[3] India proposes retaliatory duties at WTO against U.S. tariffs on autos, https://www.theglobeandmail.com/business/article-india-retaliatory-tariffs-us-autos-wto/

**Topic 2.2: U.S. Diplomacy with Russia & Ukraine**
Two critical and seemingly intertwined events have occurred simultaneously. Russia has launched what is being described as its "largest aerial attack" against Ukraine, deploying a record number of drones [1]. This major military escalation took place during the same period that President Trump reportedly held separate telephone conversations with both Ukrainian President Volodymyr Zelenskyy and Russian President Vladimir Putin [2]. The precise nature and timing of these diplomatic discussions in relation to the attacks remain unclear based on the headlines.

**References:**
[1] Russia hits Ukraine with largest aerial attack as Trump talks to Zelenskyy and Putin, https://www.npr.org/2025/07/04/nx-s1-5456846/russia-hits-ukraine-with-largest-aerial-attack-as-trump-talks-to-zelenskyy-and-putin

[2] Russia launches record number of drones at Ukraine after latest Trump-Putin phone call, https://edition.cnn.com/2025/07/03/europe/kyiv-ukraine-strikes-trump-putin-talks-intl-hnk

**Topic 2.3: Middle East Policy & Israeli-Palestinian Conflict**
President Trump has publicly announced that a ceasefire deal between Israel and Palestinian forces in Gaza is "near" [1]. However, the same reports that carry this announcement of diplomatic progress also state that recent Israeli strikes have killed 138 Palestinians. The available information is insufficient to determine the timeline or connection between the President's statement and the lethal strikes on the ground.

**References:**
[1] Trump says ceasefire deal is near as Israeli strikes kill 138 Palestinians in Gaza, https://www.npr.org/2025/07/04/nx-s1-5456983/trump-says-ceasefire-deal-near-israeli-strikes-kill-138-palestinians-gaza

**Topic 2.4: Relations with Allies & International Data Sharing**
Evidence of growing friction in the U.S.-Canada relationship is emerging. The U.S. ambassador to Canada has publicly refused to commit to finalizing a new trade agreement by the previously set July 21 target date [1]. In a separate but related development, a Canadian government report concluded that the country "can no longer rely on U.S. for infectious disease data," signaling a significant breakdown in a critical area of cross-border scientific and public health cooperation [2].

**References:**
[1] U.S. ambassador won’t commit to new Canada-U.S. trade deal by July 21, https://www.ctvnews.ca/ottawa/article/us-ambassador-wont-commit-to-new-canada-us-trade-deal-by-july-21/

[2] Canada can no longer rely on U.S. for infectious disease data: report, https://ottawacitizen.com/news/local-news/canada-faces-crisis-in-communicable-disease-can-no-longer-rely-on-u-s-for-data-cmaj

**AREA 3: LEGAL, JUDICIAL, & CIVIL RIGHTS**

**Topic 3.1: Supreme Court Rulings & Actions**
The Supreme Court has issued two significant rulings with broad social implications. The Court rejected an effort by the state of Montana to revive a restrictive parental consent law for abortion access [1]. In a separate case affecting education policy, a Supreme Court decision now permits parents to opt their children out of public school lessons that include LGBTQ+ subject matter [2]. A broader analysis published in the Washington Post argues that these decisions are part of a larger pattern in which both the Supreme Court and Congress are actively ceding power to the executive branch "under Trump" [3].

**References:**
[1] Supreme Court rebuffs Montana attempt to revive parental consent abortion law, https://thehill.com/policy/healthcare/5384083-supreme-court-declines-montana-abortion-case/

[2] SCOTUS’s decision to let parents opt kids out of LGBTQ+ lessons won’t only hurt queer students, https://www.lgbtqnation.com/2025/07/scotuss-decision-to-let-parents-opt-kids-out-of-lgbtq-lessons-wont-only-hurt-queer-students/

[3] The Supreme Court and Congress cede powers to Trump and the presidency, https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2025/07/04/executive-trump-powers-congress-supreme-court/

**Topic 3.2: Law Enforcement & Intelligence Agency Conduct**
A new report has exposed a "trio of US Treasury hacks," revealing a pattern of security breaches that is reportedly causing significant anxiety among major financial institutions [1]. Separately, reports indicate that Kash Patel and John Ratcliffe are actively working to promote and substantiate claims that the FBI and CIA were involved in a conspiracy against President Trump [2]. ## 6. Domestic Politics & Elections

### 6.1. Democratic Party Dynamics & Key Primary Races
A primary election in New York has exposed deep divisions within the Democratic party. Senator Kirsten Gillibrand has publicly apologized to candidate Zohran Mamdani after being criticized for making a "'jihad' claim" against him during the race [1]. Mamdani's subsequent victory has prompted angry "rants" from top Democratic donors about the party's direction. Among them, billionaire Bill Ackman—while directing major funding to Eric Adams in the NYC mayoral race—has also declared he is ‘ready to go to battle, guns blazing’ against Zohran Mamdani [2].

**References:**
[1] Kirsten Gillibrand apologizes to Zohran Mamdani over ‘jihad’ claim | Zohran Mamdani, https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2025/jul/02/zohran-mamdani-kirsten-gillibrand-apologizes  
[2] Bill Ackman’s ‘hundreds of millions of dollars’ in NYC mayoral race goes to Eric Adams—‘ready to go to battle, guns blazing’ against Zohran Mamdani, https://fortune.com/2025/07/03/bill-ackman-zohran-mamdani-new-york-city-mayor-race-eric-adams-andrew-cuomo/  

### 6.2. 2026 Midterm Outlook & Voting Trends
As focus begins to shift to the 2026 midterms, new federal data on voting behavior shows a significant trend. While mail-in voting rates have declined from their 2020 peak, early in-person voting has become "a hit" and is now an established preference for a large segment of the electorate [1]. Looking ahead to the House of Representatives, political analyst Chris Matthews has offered an early prediction that Democrats have a "good chance" of picking up between 15 and 20 seats [2].

**References:**
[1] Mail-in voting rates dropped but early in-person voting is a hit, federal report shows, https://www.npr.org/2025/07/01/nx-s1-5452536/mail-in-ballot-early-in-person-voting-2024-election  
[2] Chris Matthews: Democrats have good chance of picking up ’15 to 20′ House seats in midterms, https://thehill.com/homenews/media/5382685-chris-matthews-democrats-house-gains/  

### 6.3. Public Opinion, Polling, and Third-Party Influence
A new national poll suggests significant dissatisfaction with the two-party system, finding that nearly 40 percent of American voters say they would consider backing a new third party led by Elon Musk [1]. This coincides with a fractured public mood, captured by dueling opinion pieces: one from young people expressing a renewed love for America, and another comparing this year's July 4th celebration to observing an anniversary "the day after you learn that your spouse cheated on you" [2].
